# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Pod Eviction on Node Memory Pressure

## Your Task

Pods are evicted with reason 'memory pressure'. Find the Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that (1) define the memory pressure eviction thresholds and (2) implement the eviction manager's decision logic for memory-pressure-based pod eviction.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

64-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer documenting the kubernetes/kubernetes source files related to pod eviction on node memory pressure. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**Memory Pressure Threshold Definitions:**
- Located in `pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go`
- Defines `SignalMemoryAvailable` (capacity - working set)
- Defines `SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable` (allocatable - pod working set)
- Thresholds configured via `EvictionHard` and `EvictionSoft` flags

**Eviction Manager Decision Logic:**
1. **Main implementation**: `pkg/kubelet/eviction/eviction_manager.go`
   - `synchronize()` function (line 243) is the core control loop
   - Gets memory observations and evaluates thresholds
   - Ranks pods for eviction using `rankMemoryPressure()`
   - Evicts pods when thresholds are met

2. **Helper functions**: `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go`
   - `ParseThresholdConfig()` - parses threshold configuration
   - `thresholdsMet()` - evaluates if thresholds are exceeded
   - `makeSignalObservations()` - collects memory stats
   - `nodeConditions()` - maps to `v1.NodeMemoryPressure`

3. **Memory observation**: `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_others.go`
   - `makeMemoryAvailableSignalObservation()` calculates available memory from node stats

4. **Node integration**: `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_node_status.go`
   - `syncNodeStatus()` reports memory pressure via `IsUnderMemoryPressure()`

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol definitions, and an execution chain showing how the system works.

These are reported via syncNodeStatus() in pkg/kubelet/kubelet_node_status.go (line 780).\\n\\n5. **Pod Admission**: The Admit() function (line 146 in eviction_manager.go) prevents admission of best-effort pods when the node has memory pressure, allowing only guaranteed and burstable pods with memory requests.\\n\\n## Memory Observation Calculation\\n\\nMemory available is calculated in makeMemoryAvailableSignalObservation() (helpers_others.go, line 27):\\n- Available = summary.Node.Memory.AvailableBytes\\n- Capacity = AvailableBytes + WorkingSetBytes\\n\\nThreshold quantities are resolved by GetThresholdQuantity() in pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go (line 111), supporting both absolute quantities (e.g., 1Gi) and percentages.\\n\\n## Kernel Integration\\n\\nOn Linux with KernelMemcgNotification enabled, memory threshold notifiers in memory_threshold_notifier_linux.go provide efficient kernel-based cgroup memory pressure detection instead of polling.\"\n}\n",
